* TODO- Case 11: 04/19/2025 dict=AP, L=4582, hw=ardha, user=srhodes
old = demi-god
new = demigod
comment = Typo – Please note that the general usage is without the hyphen. Therefore, please consider this to be a Global Correction across all dictionaries. Definitions should be spelled according to current standards. There is no need to Honor Apte for an error in spelling. If you choose not to make this correction, please remember this: Sanskrit prides itself on saving even a "mātra"; and I say, "even a hyphen" that is not needed in the English language. Also, please note that this compound will not be used in Sanskrit in a hyphenated form such as "ardha-devaḥ", which simply proves my point. If all compounds were hyphenated in Sanskrit, then we would all be suffering from headaches.
status = PENDING
------------------------------------------------------------------------

* TODOx Case 25: 04/20/2025 dict=AP, L=4582, hw=ardha, user=srhodes
old = ddaṣadi
new = dṛṣadi
comment = Typo – You may consider to make this a Global Correction using the target search: " ddaṣadi"  ——becomes—–  " dṛṣadi" • the initial space surrounding the target search " ddaṣadi" is required to avoid ativyāpti, which I am sure will delight Andhrabharati, by my mention. The form: " ddaṣadi" in every single occurrence can only be this: " dṛṣadi" – There is no other possible correct combination of these letters.
status = PENDING
------------------------------------------------------------------------

* TODOx Case 44: 04/21/2025 dict=AP, L=4582, hw=ardha, user=srhodes
old = ardhapanchāla
new = ardhapañcāla
comment = Typo – Please note that we cannot have "partial" proper transliteration (i.e. 'ā') and "partial" secular phoneticism (i.e. 'n' and 'ch') occurring in a single word. Please consider this to be a Global correction across all dictionaries – that will save us from repeatedly making such a correction. The important point here is that the letters: "n" and "ch" are misleading, because the correct letters are: "ñ" and "c".
status = PENDING
------------------------------------------------------------------------

* TODOx Case 90: 04/25/2025 dict=AP, L=4662, hw=alam, user=srhodes
old = -dhūma a. [alamatyartho dhūmaḥ] thick smoke, volume of smoke.
new = -dhūma m. [alamatyartho dhūmaḥ] thick smoke, volume of smoke.
comment = Typo – Please note that this is a suggested "print change", following MW dictionary and the following reasoning: "dhūma" is masculine in gender. Here we have substantive that simply is "thick smoke". If something "has thick smoke", then THAT is another matter. But for jiust "thick smoke" itself (as cited here), the gender should be stated as masculine.
status = PENDING
** pc: 4662<pc>0233-2<k1>alam : -DUma a. : -DUma m.

* TODOx Case 533: 06/12/2025 dict=AP, L=6157, hw=asura, user=srhodes
old = Sukrāchārya

comment = Typo – Please note that we cannot have "partial" proper transliteration (i.e. 'ā') and "partial" secular phoneticism (i.e. 'S' and 'ch') occurring in a single word. Please consider this to be a Global correction across all dictionaries – that will save us from repeatedly making such a correction. The important point here is that the two letters are misleading here: "S" is misleading, because the correct letter is: "Ś" AND "ch" is misleading, because the correct letter is: "c". I have made this similar point a number of times, and I would like to here what the great Andhrabharati has to say in this regard? Does Andhrabharati agree with my correction, or is He happy with the "crass" spelling offered by Apte and others?

The Global Correction to be made uses the Target Search: "ḍk"  —— becomes —— "ṅk".  The reason that this is a safe Global correction is that although the letter combination "ṭk" is common, it will never be mistaken for "ḍk" (or vice versa). Whereas the letter combination "ḍk" is an absolute impossibility that can only be correctly rendered as: "ṅk". The obvious consideration here is the similarity between the letters "ḍ" and "ṅ" especially in regard to OCR conversion.

Please consider this to be a Global correction across all dictionaries – that will save us from repeatedly making such a correction. The important point here is that the letter "ch" is misleading, because the correct letter is: "c". I have made this similar point a number of times, and I would like to hear what the great Andhrabharati has to say in this regard? Does Andhrabharati agree with my correction, or is He happy with the "crass" spelling offered by Apte and others?
